/ <span class="geo">60.114475; -1.215874</span></span></span></a></span></li>\n<li>Scord: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Shetland&amp;params=60.142287_N_1.261629_W_"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">60&#176;08&#8242;32&#8243;N</span> <span class="longitude">1&#176;15&#8242;42&#8243;W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#65279; / &#65279;</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">60.142287&#176;N 1.261629&#176;W</span><span style="display:none">&#65279; / <span class="geo">60.142287; -1.261629</span></span></span></a></span> <a class="external autonumber" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/cowrin/3798639184" rel="nofollow">[3]</a></li>\n<li>Sullom: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Shetland&amp;params=60.439953_N_1.382306_W_"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">60&#176;26&#8242;24&#8243;N</span> <span class="longitude">1&#176;22&#8242;56&#8243;W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#65279; / &#65279;</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">60.439953&#176;N 1.382306&#176;W</span><span style="display:none">&#65279; / <span class="geo">60.439953; -1.382306</span></span></span></a></span></li>\n<li>Vatster: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Shetland&amp;params=60.212887_N_1.220861_W_"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">60&#176;12&#8242;46&#8243;N</span> <span class="longitude">1&#176;13&#8242;15&#8243;W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#65279; / &#65279;</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">60.212887&#176;N 1.220861&#176;W</span><span style="display:none">&#65279; / <span class="geo">60.212887; -1.220861</span></span></span></a></span></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loganair_Islander_at_Fair_Isle.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Loganair_Islander_at_Fair_Isle.jpg/220px-Loganair_Islander_at_Fair_Isle.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Loganair_Islander_at_Fair_Isle.jpg/330px-Loganair_Islander_at_Fair_Isle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Loganair_Islander_at_Fair_Isle.jpg/440px-Loganair_Islander_at_Fair_Isle.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Loganair_Islander_at_Fair_Isle.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Loganair" title="Loganair">Loganair</a> aircraft on <a href="/wiki/Fair_Isle" title="Fair Isle">Fair Isle</a>, midway between <a href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkney</a> and Shetland</div></div></div>\n<p>Transport between islands is primarily by ferry, and Shetland Islands Council operates various <a href="/wiki/SIC_Ferries" title="SIC Ferries">inter-island services</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[103]</a></sup> Shetland is also served by a domestic connection from Lerwick to <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a> on mainland Scotland. This service, which takes about 12 hours, is operated by <a href="/wiki/NorthLink_Ferries" title="NorthLink Ferries">NorthLink Ferries</a>. Some services also call at <a href="/wiki/Kirkwall" title="Kirkwall">Kirkwall</a>, Orkney, which increases the journey time between <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a> and Lerwick by 2 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[105]</a></sup> There are plans for road tunnels to some of the islands, especially <a href="/wiki/Bressay" title="Bressay">Bressay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whalsay" title="Whalsay">Whalsay</a>; however, it is hard to convince the mainland government to finance them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[106]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sumburgh_Airport" title="Sumburgh Airport">Sumburgh Airport</a>, the main airport on Shetland, is located close to Sumburgh Head, 40&#160;km (25&#160;mi) south of Lerwick. <a href="/wiki/Loganair" title="Loganair">Loganair</a> operates flights to other parts of Scotland up to ten times a day, the destinations being Kirkwall, Aberdeen, <a href="/wiki/Inverness" title="Inverness">Inverness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[107]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tingwall_Airport" title="Tingwall Airport">Lerwick/Tingwall Airport</a> is located 11&#160;km (6.8&#160;mi) west of Lerwick. Operated by Directflight Limited in partnership with Shetland Islands Council, it is devoted to inter-island flights from the Shetland Mainland to most of the inhabited islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[109]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Scatsta_Airport" title="Scatsta Airport">Scatsta Airport</a> near Sullom Voe allows frequent charter flights from <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_Airport" title="Aberdeen Airport">Aberdeen</a> to transport oilfield workers and this small terminal has the fifth largest number of international passengers in Scotland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[110]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Public bus services are operated on Mainland, Whalsay, Burra, Unst and Yell.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[111]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The archipelago is exposed to wind and tide, and there are numerous sites of wrecked ships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[112]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lighthouse" title="Lighthouse">Lighthouses</a> are sited as an aid to navigation at various locations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[113]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_services">Public services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Public services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Shetland_Islands_Council" title="Shetland Islands Council">Shetland Islands Council</a> is the Local Government authority for all the islands and is based in <a href="/wiki/Lerwick_Town_Hall" title="Lerwick Town Hall">Lerwick Town Hall</a>.\n</p><p>Shetland is sub-divided into 18 community council areas<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[114]</a></sup> and into 12 <a href="/wiki/List_of_civil_parishes_in_Scotland" title="List of civil parishes in Scotland">civil parishes</a> that are used for statistical purposes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[115]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="toptextcells">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td>\n<table class="wikitable title="Unst">Unst</a></small></div>\n</div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In Shetland there are two high schools&#8212;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anderson_High_School_(Lerwick,_Shetland)" title="Anderson High School (Lerwick, Shetland)">Anderson</a> and Brae&#8212;five junior high schools, and 24 primary schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[118]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Shetland is also home to the North Atlantic Fisheries College, the Centre for Nordic Studies and <a href="/wiki/Shetland_College" title="Shetland College">Shetland College</a>, which are all associated with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Highlands_and_Islands" title="University of the Highlands and Islands">University of the Highlands and Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[120]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The islands are represented by the <a href="/wiki/Shetland_football_team" title="Shetland football team">Shetland football team</a> who regularly compete in the <a href="/wiki/Island_Games" title="Island Games">Island Games</a>. The islands\' senior football league is the G&amp;S Flooring Premier League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[121]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Churches_and_religion">Churches and religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Churches and religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" (2011)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Area_Profiles_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-Area_Profiles-131">[122]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; (29.9%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic religions (1.1%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; (8.5%)</div>\n</div>\n</div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haroldswick_Methodist_Church.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="248" data-file-width="432" decoding="async" height="115" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Haroldswick_Methodist_Church.jpg/300px-Haroldswick_Methodist_Church.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Haroldswick_Methodist_Church.jpg/400px-Haroldswick_Methodist_Church.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haroldswick_Methodist_Church.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Haroldswick" title="Haroldswick">Haroldswick</a> Methodist Church, the most northerly church building in the UK</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Victoria_pier,_Lerwick_-_geograph.org.uk_-_908540.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Victoria_pier%2C_Lerwick_-_geograph.org.uk_-_908540.jpg/200px-Victoria_pier%2C_Lerwick_-_geograph.org.uk_-_908540.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Victoria_pier%2C_Lerwick_-_geograph.org.uk_-_908540.jpg/300px-Victoria_pier%2C_Lerwick_-_geograph.org.uk_-_908540.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Victoria_pier%2C_Lerwick_-_geograph.org.uk_-_908540.jpg/400px-Victoria_pier%2C_Lerwick_-_geograph.org.uk_-_908540.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Victoria_pier,_Lerwick_-_geograph.org.uk_-_908540.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lerwick</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">Reformation</a> reached the archipelago in 1560. This was an apparently peaceful transition and there is little evidence of religious intolerance in Shetland\'s recorded history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[123]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 2011 census, Shetland registered a higher proportion of people with no religion than the Scottish average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Area_Profiles_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-Area_Profiles-131">[122]</a></sup>  Nevertheless, a variety of religious denominations are represented in the islands.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Church_of_Great_Britain" title="Methodist Church of Great Britain">Methodist Church</a> has a relatively high membership in Shetland, which is a District of the Methodist Church (with the rest of Scotland comprising a separate District).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[124]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a> has a <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_polity" title="Presbyterian polity">Presbytery</a> of Shetland that includes <a href="/wiki/Lerwick_and_Bressay_Parish_Church" title="Lerwick and Bressay Parish Church">St. Columba\'s Church</a> in Lerwick.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[125]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> population is served by the church of St. Margaret and the Sacred Heart in Lerwick. The Parish is part of the Diocese of Aberdeen.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Episcopal_Church" title="Scottish Episcopal Church">Scottish Episcopal Church</a> (part of the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Communion" title="Anglican Communion">Anglican Communion</a>) has regular worship at St Magnus\' Church, Lerwick, St Colman\'s Church, Burravoe, and the Chapel of Christ the Encompasser, Fetlar, the last of which is maintained by the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Our_Lady_of_the_Isles" title="Society of Our Lady of the Isles">Society of Our Lady of the Isles</a>, the most northerly and remote <a href="/wiki/Anglican_religious_order" title="Anglican religious order">Anglican religious order</a> of nuns.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> has a congregation in Lerwick. The former print works and offices of the local newspaper, The Shetland Times, has been converted into a chapel.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Shetland is represented in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" title="British House of Commons">House of Commons</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Orkney_and_Shetland_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Orkney and Shetland (UK Parliament constituency)">Orkney and Shetland</a> <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_constituencies" title="United Kingdom constituencies">constituency</a>, which elects one <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" title="Member of Parliament">Member of Parliament</a>. Since <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2001_UK_general_election" title="2001 UK general election">2001</a>, the MP has been <a href="/wiki/Alistair_Carmichael" title="Alistair Carmichael">Alistair Carmichael</a>. This seat has been held by the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> or their predecessors the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(UK)" title="Liberal Party (UK)">Liberal Party</a> since <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1950_UK_general_election" title="1950 UK general election">1950</a>, longer than any other seat in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[128]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> the <a href="/wiki/Shetland_(Scottish_Parliament_constituency)" title="Shetland (Scottish Parliament constituency)">Shetland</a> constituency elects one <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Scottish_Parliament" title="Member of the Scottish Parliament">Member of the Scottish Parliament</a> (MSP) by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plurality_voting_system" title="Plurality voting system">first past the post</a> system. <a href="/wiki/Tavish_Scott" title="Tavish Scott">Tavish Scott</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Liberal_Democrats" title="Scottish Liberal Democrats">Scottish Liberal Democrats</a> has held the seat since the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> in 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[129]</a></sup> Shetland is within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highlands_and_Islands_(Scottish_Parliament_region)" title="Highlands and Islands (Scottish Parliament region)">Highlands and Islands</a> <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_constituencies_and_regions" title="Scottish Parliament constituencies and regions">electoral region</a>.\n</p><p>The political composition of the Shetland Islands Council is 21 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independent_(politician)" title="Independent (politician)">Independents</a> and 1 <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[130]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Wir_Shetland" title="Wir Shetland">Wir Shetland</a> movement was set up in 2015 to campaign for greater autonomy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[131]</a></sup> As of early 2018, however, the movement appears to be inactive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[133]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Shetland_flag">Shetland flag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Shetland flag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Roy Gr&#246;nneberg, who founded the local chapter of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> in 1966, designed the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Shetland" title="Flag of Shetland">flag of Shetland</a> in cooperation with Bill Adams to mark the 500th anniversary of the transfer of the islands from Norway to Scotland. The colours are identical to those of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Scotland" title="Flag of Scotland">flag of Scotland</a>, but are shaped in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nordic_cross" title="Nordic cross">Nordic cross</a>. After several unsuccessful attempts, including a <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">plebiscite</a> in 1985, the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Lyon_King_of_Arms" title="Lord Lyon King of Arms">Lord Lyon King of Arms</a> approved it as the official flag of Shetland in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flag_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-flag-143">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[Note 10]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_culture_and_the_arts">Local culture and the arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Local culture and the arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shetland_crofthouse_museum.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Shetland_crofthouse_museum.jpg/200px-Shetland_crofthouse_museum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Shetland_crofthouse_museum.jpg/300px-Shetland_crofthouse_museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Shetland_crofthouse_museum.jpg/400px-Shetland_crofthouse_museum.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shetland_crofthouse_museum.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Shetland <a href="/wiki/Croft_(land)" title="Croft (land)">Crofthouse</a> museum</div></div></div>\n<p>After the islands were transferred to Scotland, thousands of Scots families emigrated to Shetland in the 16th and 17th centuries but studies of the genetic makeup of the islands\' population indicate that Shetlanders are just under half Scandinavian in origin. A sizeable component of Scandinavian patrilineal ancestry has been reported in Orkney (55%) and Shetland (68%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goodacre_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-Goodacre-56">[51]</a></sup> This combination is reflected in many aspects of local life. For example, almost every place name in use can be traced back to the Vikings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[135]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Norn_language" title="Norn language">Norn language</a> was a form of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Norse_language" title="Old Norse language">Old Norse</a>, which continued to be spoken until the 18th century when it was replaced by an insular dialect of <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a> known as Shetlandic, which is in turn being replaced by <a href="/wiki/Scottish_English" title="Scottish English">Scottish English</a>. Although Norn was spoken for hundreds of years it is now extinct and few written sources remain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[136]</a></sup> Shetlandic is used both in local radio and dialect writing, and kept alive by organisations such as <a class="external text" href="https://www.shetlanddialect.org.uk/" rel="nofollow">Shetland Forwirds</a>, <a class="external text" href="http://www.islefolk.co" rel="nofollow">Isle Folk</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Shetland_Folk_Society" title="Shetland Folk Society">Shetland Folk Society</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[139]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Lerwick <a href="/wiki/Up_Helly_Aa" title="Up Helly Aa">Up Helly Aa</a> is one of several fire festivals held in Shetland annually in the middle of winter&#8212;it is always started on the last Tuesday of January.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[140]</a></sup> The festival is just over 100 years old in its present, highly organised form. Originally, a festival held to break up the long nights of winter and mark the end of <a href="/wiki/Yule" title="Yule">Yule</a>, the festival has become one celebrating the isles\' heritage and includes a procession of men dressed as Vikings and the burning of a replica <a href="/wiki/Longship" title="Longship">longship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[141]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UpHellyAa3(AnneBurgess)30Jan1973.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="420" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/UpHellyAa3%28AnneBurgess%2930Jan1973.jpg/220px-UpHellyAa3%28AnneBurgess%2930Jan1973.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/UpHellyAa3%28AnneBurgess%2930Jan1973.jpg/330px-UpHellyAa3%28AnneBurgess%2930Jan1973.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/UpHellyAa3%28AnneBurgess%2930Jan1973.jpg/440px-UpHellyAa3%28AnneBurgess%2930Jan1973.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UpHellyAa3(AnneBurgess)30Jan1973.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Lerwick" title="Lerwick">Lerwick</a> <a href="/wiki/Up_Helly_Aa" title="Up Helly Aa">Up Helly Aa</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cuisine" title="Cuisine">cuisine</a> of Shetland is based on locally produced lamb, beef and seafood, much of it <a href="/wiki/Organic_food" title="Organic food">organic</a>. Inevitably, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_ale" title="Real ale">real ale</a>-producing <a href="/wiki/Valhalla_Brewery" title="Valhalla Brewery">Valhalla Brewery</a> is the most northerly in Britain. The Shetland Black is a variety of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue_potato" title="Blue potato">blue potato</a> with a dark skin and indigo coloured flesh markings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[142]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Shetland competes in the biennial <a href="/wiki/International_Island_Games_Association" title="International Island Games Association">International Island Games</a>, which it hosted in <a href="/wiki/2005_Island_Games" title="2005 Island Games">2005</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[143]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Shetland\'s culture and landscapes have inspired a variety of musicians, writers and film-makers. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Forty_Fiddlers" title="The Forty Fiddlers">The Forty Fiddlers</a> was formed in the 1950s to promote the traditional fiddle style, which is a vibrant part of local culture today.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[144]</a></sup> Notable exponents of Shetland folk music include <a href="/wiki/Aly_Bain" title="Aly Bain">Aly Bain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fiddlers%27_Bid" title="Fiddlers\' Bid">Fiddlers\' Bid</a>, and the late <a href="/wiki/Tom_Anderson_(fiddler)" title="Tom Anderson (fiddler)">Tom Anderson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peerie_Willie_Johnson" title="Peerie Willie Johnson">Peerie Willie Johnson</a>. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Fraser_(singer)" title="Thomas Fraser (singer)">Thomas Fraser</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">country musician</a> who never released a commercial recording during his life, but whose work has become popular more than 20 years after his untimely death in 1978.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[145]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Writers">Writers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Writers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Walter_Scott" title="Walter Scott">Walter Scott</a>\'s 1822 novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Pirate_(novel)" title="The Pirate (novel)">The Pirate</a></i> is set in "a remote part of Shetland", and was inspired by his 1814 visit to the islands. The name <i>Jarlshof</i> meaning "Earl\'s Mansion" is a coinage of his.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaz_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaz-156">[146]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Cowie" title="Robert Cowie">Robert Cowie</a>, a doctor born in Lerwick published the 1874 work <cite class="citation book"><a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/shetlanddescrip01cowigoog" rel="nofollow"><i>Shetland: Descriptive and Historical; Being a Graduation Thesis on the Inhabitants of the Shetland Islands; and a Topographical Description of the Country</i></a>. Menzies. 1874.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Shetland%3A+Descriptive+and+Historical%3B+Being+a+Graduation+Thesis+on+the+Inhabitants+of+the+Shetland+Islands%3B+and+a+Topographical+Description+of+the+Country&amp;rft.pub=Menzies&amp;rft.date=1874&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Farchive.org%2Fdetails%2Fshetlanddescrip01cowigoog&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AShetland"></span><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r879151008">.mw-parser-output cite.citation{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .citation q{quotes:"\\"""\\"""\'""\'"}.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-free a{background:url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Lock-green.svg/9px-Lock-green.svg.png")no-repeat;background-position:right .1em center}.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-limited a,.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-registration a{background:url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Lock-gray-alt-2.svg/9px-Lock-gray-alt-2.svg.png")no-repeat;background-position:right .1em center}.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-subscription a{background:url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Lock-red-alt-2.svg/9px-Lock-red-alt-2.svg.png")no-repeat;background-position:right .1em center}.mw-parser-output .cs1-subscription,.mw-parser-output .cs1-registration{color:#555}.mw-parser-output .cs1-subscription span,.mw-parser-output .cs1-registration span{border-bottom:1px dotted;cursor:help}.mw-parser-output .cs1-ws-icon a{background:url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/12px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png")no-repeat;background-position:right .1em center}.mw-parser-output code.cs1-code{color:inherit;background:inherit;border:inherit;padding:inherit}.mw-parser-output .cs1-hidden-error{display:none;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-visible-error{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-maint{display:none;color:#33aa33;margin-left:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .cs1-subscription,.mw-parser-output .cs1-registration,.mw-parser-output .cs1-format{font-size:95%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-left,.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-wl-left{padding-left:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-right,.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-wl-right{padding-right:0.2em}</style>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hugh_MacDiarmid" title="Hugh MacDiarmid">Hugh MacDiarmid</a>, the Scots poet and writer lived in Whalsay from the mid-1930s through 1942, and wrote many poems there, including a number that directly address or reflect the Shetland environment such as "On A Raised Beach", which was inspired by a visit to <a href="/wiki/West_Linga" title="West Linga">West Linga</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[147]</a></sup> The 1975 novel <i>North Star</i> by <a href="/wiki/Hammond_Innes" title="Hammond Innes">Hammond Innes</a> is largely set in Shetland and <a href="/wiki/Raman_Mundair" title="Raman Mundair">Raman Mundair</a>\'s 2007 book of poetry <i>A Choreographer\'s Cartography</i> offers a British Asian perspective on the landscape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[148]</a></sup> The <i>Shetland Quartet</i> by <a href="/wiki/Ann_Cleeves" title="Ann Cleeves">Ann Cleeves</a>, who previously lived in <a href="/wiki/Fair_Isle" title="Fair Isle">Fair Isle</a>, is a series of crime novels set around the islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[149]</a></sup> In 2013 her novel <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Bones" title="Red Bones">Red Bones</a></i> became the basis of <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> crime drama television series <i><a href="/wiki/Shetland_(TV_series)" title="Shetland (TV series)">Shetland</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[150]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Vagaland" title="Vagaland">Vagaland</a>, who grew up in Walls, was arguably Shetland\'s finest poet of the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[151]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Haldane_Burgess" title="Haldane Burgess">Haldane Burgess</a> was a Shetland historian, poet, novelist, violinist, linguist and socialist and <a href="/wiki/Rhoda_Bulter" title="Rhoda Bulter">Rhoda Bulter</a> (1929&#8211;94) is one of the best-known Shetland poets of recent times. Other 20th and 21st century poets and novelists include <a href="/wiki/Christine_De_Luca" title="Christine De Luca">Christine De Luca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Alan_Jamieson" title="Robert Alan Jamieson">Robert Alan Jamieson</a> who grew up in <a href="/wiki/Sandness" title="Sandness">Sandness</a>, the late <a href="/wiki/Lollie_Graham" title="Lollie Graham">Lollie Graham</a> of <a href="/wiki/Veensgarth" title="Veensgarth">Veensgarth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stella_Sutherland" title="Stella Sutherland">Stella Sutherland</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bressay" title="Bressay">Bressay</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[152]</a></sup> the late William J Tait from Yell<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[153]</a></sup> and Laureen Johnson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[154]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are two monthly magazines in production: <i>Shetland Life</i> and <i>i\'i\' Shetland</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[156]</a></sup>  The quarterly <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Shetlander" title="The New Shetlander">The New Shetlander</a></i>, founded in 1947, is said to be Scotland\'s longest-running literary magazine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[157]</a></sup> For much of the later 20th century it was the major vehicle for the work of local writers &#8212; and others, including early work by <a href="/wiki/George_Mackay_Brown" title="George Mackay Brown">George Mackay Brown</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[158]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Films_and_television">Films and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Films and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Michael_Powell" title="Michael Powell">Michael Powell</a> made <i><a href="/wiki/The_Edge_of_the_World" title="The Edge of the World">The Edge of the World</a></i> in 1937, a dramatisation based on the true story of the evacuation of the last 36 inhabitants of the remote island of <a href="/wiki/St_Kilda,_Scotland" title="St Kilda, Scotland">St Kilda</a> on 29 August 1930. St Kilda lies in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, 1.466 kilometres (0.911&#160;mi) west of the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Hebrides" title="Outer Hebrides">Outer Hebrides</a> but Powell was unable to get permission to film there. Undaunted, he made the film over four months during the summer of 1936 on Foula and the film transposes these events to Shetland. Forty years later, the documentary <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Return_to_the_Edge_of_the_World" title="Return to the Edge of the World">Return to the Edge of the World</a></i> was filmed, capturing a reunion of cast and crew of the film as they revisited the island in 1978.\n</p><p>A number of other films have been made on or about Shetland including <i>A Crofter\'s Life in Shetland</i> (1932)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[159]</a></sup> <i>A Shetland Lyric</i> (1934),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[160]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Devil%27s_Gate_(film)" title="Devil\'s Gate (film)">Devil\'s Gate</a></i> (2003) and <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_Nice_Up_North" title="It\'s Nice Up North">It\'s Nice Up North</a></i> (2006), a comedy documentary by <a href="/wiki/Graham_Fellows" title="Graham Fellows">Graham Fellows</a>. An annual film festival takes place in the newly built <a href="/wiki/Mareel" title="Mareel">Mareel</a>, a cinema, music and education venue.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/BBC_One" title="BBC One">BBC One</a> television series <i><a href="/wiki/Shetland_(TV_series)" title="Shetland (TV series)">Shetland</a></i>, a crime drama, is set on the islands and is based on the book series by <a href="/wiki/Ann_Cleeves" title="Ann Cleeves">Ann Cleeves</a>. The programme is filmed partly on Shetland and partly on the Scottish mainland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[162]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Shetland has three <a href="/wiki/National_nature_reserve_(United_Kingdom)" title="National nature reserve (United Kingdom)">national nature reserves</a>, at the seabird colonies of <a href="/wiki/Hermaness" title="Hermaness">Hermaness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Noss" title="Noss">Noss</a>, and at <a href="/wiki/Keen_of_Hamar" title="Keen of Hamar">Keen of Hamar</a> to preserve the <a href="/wiki/Serpentine_soil" title="Serpentine soil">serpentine</a> flora. There are a further 81 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SSSIs" title="SSSIs">SSSIs</a>, which cover 66% or more of the land surfaces of Fair Isle, Papa Stour, Fetlar, Noss and Foula. Mainland has 45 separate sites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SIC52_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-SIC52-173">[163]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Edmondston%27s_Chickweed,_Keen_of_Hamar_CRW_2437.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="427" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Edmondston%27s_Chickweed%2C_Keen_of_Hamar_CRW_2437.JPG/220px-Edmondston%27s_Chickweed%2C_Keen_of_Hamar_CRW_2437.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Edmondston%27s_Chickweed%2C_Keen_of_Hamar_CRW_2437.JPG/330px-Edmondston%27s_Chickweed%2C_Keen_of_Hamar_CRW_2437.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Edmondston%27s_Chickweed%2C_Keen_of_Hamar_CRW_2437.JPG/440px-Edmondston%27s_Chickweed%2C_Keen_of_Hamar_CRW_2437.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Edmondston%27s_Chickweed,_Keen_of_Hamar_CRW_2437.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shetland_mouse-ear" title="Shetland mouse-ear">Shetland mouse-ear</a> (<i>Cerastium nigrescens</i>), on the <a href="/wiki/Keen_of_Hamar" title="Keen of Hamar">Keen of Hamar</a> reserve, <a href="/wiki/Unst" title="Unst">Unst</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora">Flora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Flora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The landscape in Shetland is marked by the grazing of <a href="/wiki/Sheep" title="Sheep">sheep</a> and the harsh conditions have limited the total number of plant species to about 400.  Native <a href="/wiki/Tree" title="Tree">trees</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Sorbus_aucuparia" title="Sorbus aucuparia">rowan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malus_sylvestris" title="Malus sylvestris">crab apple</a> are only found in a few isolated places such as cliffs and loch islands.  The flora is dominated by Arctic-alpine plants, wild flowers, <a href="/wiki/Moss" title="Moss">moss</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lichen" title="Lichen">lichen</a>. <a href="/wiki/Scilla_verna" title="Scilla verna">Spring squill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plantago_coronopus" title="Plantago coronopus">buck\'s-horn plantain</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scots_lovage" title="Scots lovage">Scots lovage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhodiola_rosea" title="Rhodiola rosea">roseroot</a> and <a href="/wiki/Silene_uniflora" title="Silene uniflora">sea campion</a> are abundant, especially in sheltered places.  Shetland mouse-ear (<i><a href="/wiki/Cerastium_nigrescens" title="Cerastium nigrescens">Cerastium nigrescens</a></i>) is an <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> flowering plant found only in Shetland. It was first recorded in 1837 by botanist <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edmondston" title="Thomas Edmondston">Thomas Edmondston</a>.  Although reported from two other sites in the nineteenth century, it currently grows only on two serpentine hills on the island of Unst. The nationally scarce <a href="/wiki/Mertensia" title="Mertensia">oysterplant</a> is found on several islands and the British <a href="/wiki/IUCN_Red_List" title="IUCN Red List">Red Listed</a> <a href="/wiki/Bryophyte" title="Bryophyte">bryophyte</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Thamnobryum" title="Thamnobryum">Thamnobryum alopecurum</a></i> has also been recorded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[167]</a></sup> Listed marine algae include: <i><a href="/wiki/Polysiphonia_fibrillosa" title="Polysiphonia fibrillosa">Polysiphonia fibrillosa</a></i> (Dillwyn) Sprengel, <i><a href="/wiki/Polysiphonia_atlantica" title="Polysiphonia atlantica">Polysiphonia atlantica</a></i> Kapraun and J.Norris, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polysiphonia_brodiaei" title="Polysiphonia brodiaei">Polysiphonia brodiaei</a></i> (Dillwyn) Sprengel, <i><a href="/wiki/Polysiphonia_elongata" title="Polysiphonia elongata">Polysiphonia elongata</a></i> (Hudson) Sprengel, <i><a href="/wiki/Polysiphonia_elongella" title="Polysiphonia elongella">Polysiphonia elongella</a></i>. Harvey <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[168]</a></sup> The Shetland Monkeyflower is unique to Shetland and is a mutation of the <a href="/wiki/Erythranthe" title="Erythranthe">Monkeyflower</a> <i>(mimulus guttatus</i>) introduced to Shetland in the 19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[170]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">Fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Shetland has numerous seabird colonies. Birds found on the islands include <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_puffin" title="Atlantic puffin">Atlantic puffin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Storm-petrel" title="Storm-petrel">storm-petrel</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red-throated_diver" title="Red-throated diver">red-throated diver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_gannet" title="Northern gannet">northern gannet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_skua" title="Great skua">great skua</a> (locally called the "bonxie").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SNH_2008_p._16_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-SNH_2008_p._16-181">[171]</a></sup> Numerous rarities have also been recorded including <a href="/wiki/Black-browed_albatross" title="Black-browed albatross">black-browed albatross</a> and <a href="/wiki/Snow_goose" title="Snow goose">snow goose</a>, and a single pair of <a href="/wiki/Snowy_owl" title="Snowy owl">snowy owls</a> bred on Fetlar from 1967 to 1975.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SNH_2008_p._16_181-1"><a href="#cite_note-SNH_2008_p._16-181">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guinn_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guinn-182">[172]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[173]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Shetland_wren" title="Shetland wren">Shetland wren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fair_Isle_wren" title="Fair Isle wren">Fair Isle wren</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland_starling&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Shetland starling (page does not exist)">Shetland starling</a> are subspecies <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> to Shetland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[174]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Endemic_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-Endemic-185">[175]</a></sup> There are also populations of various moorland birds such as <a href="/wiki/Curlew" title="Curlew">curlew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snipe" title="Snipe">snipe</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurasian_golden_plover" title="Eurasian golden plover">golden plover</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[176]</a></sup>\n</p><p>One of the early <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ornithologist" title="Ornithologist">ornithologists</a> that wrote about the wealth of birdlife on the Shetlands was <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Selous" title="Edmund Selous">Edmund Selous</a> (1857-1934) in his book <i>The Bird Watcher in the Shetlands</i> (1905).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-selous_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-selous-187">[177]</a></sup> He writes extensively about the gulls and terns, about the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arctic_skua" title="Arctic skua">lesser or arctic skuas</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Black_guillemot" title="Black guillemot">black guillemots</a> and many other birds (and the seals) of the islands.\n</p><p>The geographical isolation and recent glacial history of Shetland have resulted in a depleted mammalian fauna and the <a href="/wiki/Brown_rat" title="Brown rat">brown rat</a> and <a href="/wiki/House_mouse" title="House mouse">house mouse</a> are two of only three species of rodent present on the islands. The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland_field_mouse&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Shetland field mouse (page does not exist)">Shetland field mouse</a> is the third and the archipelago\'s fourth endemic subspecies, of which there are three varieties on Yell, Foula and Fair Isle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Endemic_185-1"><a href="#cite_note-Endemic-185">[175]</a></sup> They are variants of <i><a href="/wiki/Wood_mouse" title="Wood mouse">Apodemus sylvaticus</a></i> and archaeological evidence suggests that this species was present during the Middle <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> (around 200 BC to AD 400). It is possible that <i>Apodemus</i> was introduced from Orkney where a population has existed since at the least the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[178]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domesticated_animals">Domesticated animals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Domesticated animals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shetland_Pony1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Shetland_Pony1.jpg/220px-Shetland_Pony1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Shetland_Pony1.jpg/330px-Shetland_Pony1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Shetland_Pony1.jpg/440px-Shetland_Pony1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shetland_Pony1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Shetland pony</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Shetland_animal_breeds" title="Shetland animal breeds">Shetland animal breeds</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_domesticated_Scottish_breeds" title="List of domesticated Scottish breeds">List of domesticated Scottish breeds</a></div>\n<p>There is a variety of indigenous breeds, of which the diminutive <a href="/wiki/Shetland_pony" title="Shetland pony">Shetland pony</a> is probably the best known, as well as being an important part of the Shetland farming tradition.  The first written record of the pony was in 1603 in the Court Books of Shetland and, for its size, it is the strongest of all the horse breeds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spsbs_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-spsbs-189">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[180]</a></sup>  Others are the <a href="/wiki/Shetland_Sheepdog" title="Shetland Sheepdog">Shetland Sheepdog</a> or "Sheltie", the endangered <a href="/wiki/Shetland_cattle" title="Shetland cattle">Shetland cattle</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[181]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shetland_Goose" title="Shetland Goose">Shetland Goose</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[183]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Shetland_sheep" title="Shetland sheep">Shetland sheep</a> which is believed to have originated prior to 1000 AD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[184]</a></sup>  The <a href="/wiki/Grice" title="Grice">Grice</a> was a breed of semi-domesticated pig that had a habit of attacking lambs, and that became extinct in 1930.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[185]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">\n<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="flag" class="noviewer thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="19" data-file-width="200" decoding="async" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Ic%C3%B4ne_Ile.svg/28px-Ic%C3%B4ne_Ile.svg.png" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Ic%C3%B4ne_Ile.svg/56px-Ic%C3%B4ne_Ile.svg.png 2x" width="28"/></a></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Islands" title="Portal:Islands">Islands portal</a></span></li></ul></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lists">Lists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Lists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of counties of the United Kingdom">List of counties of the United Kingdom</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_islands" title="List of islands">List of islands</a></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="About_Shetland">About Shetland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: About Shetland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Mavis_Grind" title="Mavis Grind">Mavis Grind</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Udal_law" title="Udal law">Udal law</a></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><i lang="no" title="Norwegian language text"><a href="/wiki/Hjeltefjorden" title="Hjeltefjorden">Hjeltefjorden</a></i></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Florv%C3%A5g" title="Battle of Florv&#229;g">Battle of Florv&#229;g</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/R%C3%B6gnvald_Kali_Kolsson" title="R&#246;gnvald Kali Kolsson">R&#246;gnvald Kali Kolsson</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_prehistoric_Scotland" title="Timeline of prehistoric Scotland">Timeline of prehistoric Scotland</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Scotland" title="Prehistoric Scotland">Prehistoric Scotland</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Constitutional_status_of_Orkney,_Shetland_and_the_Western_Isles" title="Constitutional status of Orkney, Shetland and the Western Isles">Constitutional status of Orkney, Shetland and the Western Isles</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Watson (1926) is sure that Tacitus was referring to Shetland, although Breeze (2002) is more sceptical. Thule is first mentioned by <a href="/wiki/Pytheas" title="Pytheas">Pytheas</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Massilia" title="Massilia">Massilia</a> when he visited Britain sometime between 322 and 285 BC, but it is unlikely he meant Shetland as he believed it was six days sail north of Britain and one day from the frozen sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Breeze_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Breeze-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scots_Gaelic" title="Scots Gaelic">Scots Gaelic</a> name for Shetland, <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Sealtainn</i> <small></small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Help:IPA/Scottish Gaelic">[&#712;&#643;al&#736;&#810;t&#810;&#618;&#626;]</a></span> is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a> <a href="/wiki/Dative_case" title="Dative case">dative</a> form <i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">Hjaltlandi</i> through, as in Scots <i>Shetland</i>, the process of <a href="/wiki/Lenition" title="Lenition">reverse lenition</a> of the initial <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/hj/</span> to <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/&#643;/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> In contrast with Scots, Gaelic has preserved the first <i>l</i> (in <i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">hjalt</i>), but the last one (in <i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">land</i>) is disappeared.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As with all western dialects of Norse, the stressed <i>a</i> shifts to <i>e</i> and so the <i>ja</i> became <i>je</i> as with Norse <i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">hjalpa</i> which became <i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">hjelpa</i>. Then the pronunciation changed through a process of <a href="/wiki/Lenition" title="Lenition">reverse lenition</a> of the initial <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/hj/</span> to <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/&#643;/</span>. This is also found in some Norwegian dialects in for instance the word hj&#229; (with) and the place names <a href="/wiki/Hjerkinn" title="Hjerkinn">Hjerkinn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sjoa" title="Sjoa">Sjoa</a> (from <i>*Hj&#243;</i>). Lastly the <i>l</i> before the <i>t</i> disappeared.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-&#229;_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-&#229;-6">[6]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Shetland Islands Council state there are 15 inhabited islands, and count East and West Burra, which are joined by a bridge, as a single unit. Out Skerries has two inhabited islands: <a href="/wiki/Housay" title="Housay">Housay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bruray" title="Bruray">Bruray</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SIC4_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-SIC4-1">[1]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-46">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Scord of Brouster site includes a cluster of six or seven walled fields and three stone circular houses that contains the earliest <a href="/wiki/Hoe_(tool)" title="Hoe (tool)">hoe</a>-blades found so far in Scotland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[41]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-58"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-58">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Some scholars believe that this story, which appears in the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orkneyinga_Saga" title="Orkneyinga Saga">Orkneyinga Saga</a></i> is apocryphal and based on the later voyages of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magnus_III_of_Norway" title="Magnus III of Norway">Magnus Barelegs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[52]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-72"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-72">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Apparently without the knowledge of the Norwegian <i lang="no" title="Norwegian language text"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rigsraadet" title="Rigsraadet">Rigsraadet</a></i> (Council of the Realm), Christian pawned Orkney for 50,000 Rhenish <a href="/wiki/Guilder" title="Guilder">guilders</a>. On 28 May the next year, he also pawned Shetland for 8,000 Rhenish guilders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[64]</a></sup> He had secured a clause in the contract which gave future kings of Norway the right to redeem the islands for a fixed sum of 210&#160;kg of gold or 2,310&#160;kg of silver. Several attempts were made during the 17th and 18th centuries to redeem the islands, without success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[65]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-75">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">When Norway became independent again in 1906, the Shetland authorities sent a letter to King <a href="/wiki/Haakon_VII_of_Norway" title="Haakon VII of Norway">Haakon VII</a> in which they stated: "Today no \'foreign\' flag is more familiar or more welcome in our voes and havens than that of Norway, and Shetlanders continue to look upon Norway as their mother-land, and recall with pride and affection the time when their forefathers were under the rule of the Kings of Norway."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sch13_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sch13-62">[56]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-98"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-98">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">No other part of the UK has any such oil-related fund. By comparison, as of 31 December 2010 the total value of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Government_Pension_Fund_of_Norway" title="The Government Pension Fund of Norway">Government Pension Fund of Norway</a> was <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_krone" title="Norwegian krone">NOK</a> 3&#160;077 billion ($525 bn),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbim110318_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-nbim110318-97">[89]</a></sup> i.e., circa &#163;68,000 per head.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-144"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-144">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The flag is the same design Icelandic republicans used in the early 20th century known in Iceland as <i lang="is" title="Icelandic language text">Hv&#237;tbl&#225;inn</i>, the "white-blue".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flag_143-1"><a href="#cite_note-flag-143">[134]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n</ol></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shetland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 20em;
